<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_983072832">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/983072832" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl" class="left imgcol" title="Tadiana ? Night Owl?"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1383845644p2/8734459.jpg" alt="Tadiana ? Night Owl?" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/983072832?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 10, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl" class="user" title="Tadiana ? Night Owl?">Tadiana ? Night Owl?</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/222063.Stardust" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780380804559" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy-for-grownups" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy-for-grownups</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fairy-tale" class="actionLinkLite">fairy-tale</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=library-has" class="actionLinkLite">library-has</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer983072832">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer414548506620579987">Neil Gaiman and I have a love-hate relationship, and I hope that bothers him as much as it bothers me. He's a gifted writer and I keep thinking that I ought to love everything he writes, but so far his books have struck me either as: <br /><br />• so bizarre and off-putting that I couldn't get into it &lt;---<a title="American Gods (American Gods, #1) by Neil Gaiman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4407.American_Gods__American_Gods___1_">American Gods</a>,<br />• hauntingly beautiful but kind of confusing &lt;---<a title="The Ocean at the End of the Lane by Neil Gaiman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15783514.The_Ocean_at_the_End_of_the_Lane">The Ocean at the End of the Lane</a>, or<br />• having a marvelous setting but being a little on the predictable side &lt;---<a title="Neverwhere by Neil Gaiman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14497.Neverwhere">Neverwhere</a>.<br /><br />Stardust f</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText414548506620579987">Neil Gaiman and I have a love-hate relationship, and I hope that bothers him as much as it bothers me. He's a gifted writer and I keep thinking that I ought to love everything he writes, but so far his books have struck me either as: <br /><br />• so bizarre and off-putting that I couldn't get into it &lt;---<a title="American Gods (American Gods, #1) by Neil Gaiman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4407.American_Gods__American_Gods___1_">American Gods</a>,<br />• hauntingly beautiful but kind of confusing &lt;---<a title="The Ocean at the End of the Lane by Neil Gaiman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15783514.The_Ocean_at_the_End_of_the_Lane">The Ocean at the End of the Lane</a>, or<br />• having a marvelous setting but being a little on the predictable side &lt;---<a title="Neverwhere by Neil Gaiman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14497.Neverwhere">Neverwhere</a>.<br /><br />Stardust falls into the third category. In many ways it's a lovely, whimsical, humorous fairy tale, and I <em>love</em> fairy tales, so I was predisposed to like this book, but in the end I had a few issues with it.<br /><br />An English town with the mundane name of Wall lies on the boundaries of Faerie. It takes its name from the high rock wall that separates Victorian England and our world from Faerie. But there is a gap in the wall, and though men guard the gap against anyone entering or leaving Faerie from our world, every nine years there is a May Day fair when the guard is set aside . . . and sometimes the rules are broken. <br /><br />One May Day young Dunstan Thorn wanders into Faerie and is entranced by a slave girl with violet eyes and cat ears. Nine months later, a baby is unceremoniously thrust through the gap into Wall, with the name Tristran Thorn pinned to his blanket. Nearly eighteen years after that, Tristran (who has no idea of his origin) falls in love with a lovely but standoffish young girl named Victoria. Tristran begs her to kiss him, or marry him, or <em>something.</em> She demurs, and he rashly promises to bring her the treasures of the earth--including the star that they just saw fall to the earth. Victoria lightly promises him anything he desires if he will bring her the fallen star. So off Tristran goes to Faerie, to catch the fallen star. It turns out that in Faerie, stars are beautiful and somewhat sparkly young women. Unfortunately for both Tristran and the star, there are several other people who want the star as well, for reasons more dark than Tristran's.<br /><br /><img width="250" height="375" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415768415i/11843354._SY540_.jpg" /><br /><br />Although this book is written in a rather simplistic style, reminiscent of old fairy tales, this one is definitely for adults. There's a somewhat detailed sexual scene, quite a bit of gore and death, and the star drops an F-bomb when she drops to earth. If you're going to give me adult content, then give me <u>real adult content</u>: depth, details, complex world building, unexpected turns in the story. This one didn't quite hit the mark. There were several scenes and subplots that I thought begged for a more detailed description and some background: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[the little man who helps Tristran on his way, the flying ship, the man in the black silk top hat at the end (did I miss his significance somehow?) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I wanted more in-depth world building, and a plot that was less predictable.<br /><br />This is an adventurous journey through the land of Faerie, with magic, witches, enchantments, unicorns, <s>rainbows</s> . . . just about every fantastical element you've ever read in a fairy tale manages to surface somewhere or other in this book. In spite of my qualms and reservations, I still thought this was, overall, an enjoyable fairy tale with some darker elements.<br /><br /><img width="300" height="446" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415768415i/11843355._SY540_.jpg" /><br /><br />3 1/2 stars, rounding up to 4.<br /><br />Content advisory: see above. Not for kids or young teens.<!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="414548506620579987">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1163905505">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1163905505" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6206860-jean-menzies" class="left imgcol" title="Jean Menzies"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1358274654p2/6206860.jpg" alt="Jean Menzies" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1163905505?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 06, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6206860-jean-menzies" class="user" title="Jean Menzies">Jean Menzies</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/818478.Stardust" title="Paperback 9780755322824" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6206860-jean-menzies?shelf=books-i-own" class="actionLinkLite">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6206860-jean-menzies?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6206860-jean-menzies?shelf=2015-tbr" class="actionLinkLite">2015-tbr</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1163905505">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3732920624465831779">This book was my favourite read of Neil Gaiman's so far! Not that I didn't love the two I had previously read but this was also the first adult book of his that I've read and that definitely made a difference. There was no holding back and I loved the mixture of magic, adventure, intrigue and romance that surrounded this novel. Neil Gaiman is ever the clever and witty writer and this came out in a whole new way for me in this adult novel.<br /><br />Tristran lives in the town of Wall that borders the land o</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3732920624465831779">This book was my favourite read of Neil Gaiman's so far! Not that I didn't love the two I had previously read but this was also the first adult book of his that I've read and that definitely made a difference. There was no holding back and I loved the mixture of magic, adventure, intrigue and romance that surrounded this novel. Neil Gaiman is ever the clever and witty writer and this came out in a whole new way for me in this adult novel.<br /><br />Tristran lives in the town of Wall that borders the land of faery and in a quest to prove his 'love' for a young lady he crosses the wall to find a fallen star. And thus the adventure ensues. I have to say, as well, I did love Tristran, he was such an immensely likeable character. <br /><br />I would like to add that technically I would give this book a 4.5 stars rather than a 4 and only not a 5 because I can't help but wish it had been longer. The world of faery beyond the wall was so intriguing and the characters we came across were so fascinating that I wanted more, I wanted an epic fantasy novel but then maybe I'm just being greedy.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3732920624465831779">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_242094008">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/242094008" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6313408-jonathan" class="left imgcol" title="Jonathan"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1450116936p2/6313408.jpg" alt="Jonathan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/242094008?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 07, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6313408-jonathan" class="user" title="Jonathan">Jonathan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1778908.Stardust" title="Paperback 9780755337514" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan?shelf=fantasy-challenge" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy-challenge</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan?shelf=neil-gaiman" class="actionLinkLite">neil-gaiman</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan?shelf=books-with-films" class="actionLinkLite">books-with-films</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan?shelf=favourites" class="actionLinkLite">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer242094008">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16475077940281593638"><br /><em>Stardust</em> follows the adventure of one Tristran Thorn from his unusual birth through to his eventual marriage. Well this is a modern fairytale for older audiences after all. He desires to win the love of one girl called Victoria whom he names the most beautiful of all. And to win her love he must hunt down a star fallen from the sky who has ended up deep within Faerie. And so begins a most unusual adventure at once reminiscent of <a title="The Complete Grimm's Fairy Tales (Pantheon Fairy Tale and Folklore Library) by Jacob Grimm" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22917.The_Complete_Grimm_s_Fairy_Tales__Pantheon_Fairy_Tale_and_Folklore_Library_">The Complete Grimm's Fairy Tales</a>, <a title="Peter Pan by J.M. Barrie" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34268.Peter_Pan">Peter Pan</a>, <a title="Alice in Wonderland by Lewis Carroll" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13023.Alice_in_Wonderland">Alice in Wonderland</a> an</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16475077940281593638"><br /><em>Stardust</em> follows the adventure of one Tristran Thorn from his unusual birth through to his eventual marriage. Well this is a modern fairytale for older audiences after all. He desires to win the love of one girl called Victoria whom he names the most beautiful of all. And to win her love he must hunt down a star fallen from the sky who has ended up deep within Faerie. And so begins a most unusual adventure at once reminiscent of <a title="The Complete Grimm's Fairy Tales (Pantheon Fairy Tale and Folklore Library) by Jacob Grimm" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22917.The_Complete_Grimm_s_Fairy_Tales__Pantheon_Fairy_Tale_and_Folklore_Library_">The Complete Grimm's Fairy Tales</a>, <a title="Peter Pan by J.M. Barrie" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34268.Peter_Pan">Peter Pan</a>, <a title="Alice in Wonderland by Lewis Carroll" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13023.Alice_in_Wonderland">Alice in Wonderland</a> and <a title="The Chronicles of Narnia (Chronicles of Narnia #1-7) by C.S. Lewis" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11127.The_Chronicles_of_Narnia__Chronicles_of_Narnia__1_7_">The Chronicles of Narnia</a> and yet in its own way something entirely different. It was a charming book that I would highly recommend to anyone over the age of say twelve who still appreciates fairytale stories. There is a little mature content which would certainly go over the heads of young children.<br /><br />Gaiman's prose is very British in its tone - which I love. I certainly can never find fault with his writing ability, the unique mix of quirkiness, wit and fantasy which is his trademark. He did pen one of my favourite Doctor Who episodes of Series Six and I must say that all I have read of his I have enjoyed. Yet something about his work prevents me from fully loving it as I would love another similar fairytale fantasy. Either way this is a book all who have ever invested their time in fable, fairytale or mythology. It certainly is a clever, well knit book with few faults and yet for some reason hard to love. Is it simply that I find it dry and therefore it lacks that simplest of things: a full emotional resonation? </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16475077940281593638">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_47823005">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/47823005" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/88967-ben" class="left imgcol" title="Ben"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1321577354p2/88967.jpg" alt="Ben" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/47823005?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 22, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/88967-ben" class="user" title="Ben">Ben</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/88967-ben?shelf=good-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">good-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/88967-ben?shelf=read-in-2009" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2009</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/88967-ben?shelf=like-magic" class="actionLinkLite">like-magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer47823005">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3294209893180208015">I can only do fantasy novels every so often; I much prefer literature. Still, I find it important to read these things on occasion, because they provide such an excellent escape: that leap into worlds that are nothing like ours; the way they enable our going beyond ourselves and render us capable of expanding our consciousness; the way they can temporarily alter us in ways non-fantasy novels are incapable. We could all use that kind of escape once in a while.<br /><br />And <em>Stardust</em> was great for just that.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3294209893180208015">I can only do fantasy novels every so often; I much prefer literature. Still, I find it important to read these things on occasion, because they provide such an excellent escape: that leap into worlds that are nothing like ours; the way they enable our going beyond ourselves and render us capable of expanding our consciousness; the way they can temporarily alter us in ways non-fantasy novels are incapable. We could all use that kind of escape once in a while.<br /><br />And <em>Stardust</em> was great for just that. It was an easy read, never a strain; very imaginative, even at times, captivating. This was my first exposure to Gaiman and I'm left impressed: his writing was acute and flowing, his imagination, vivid; most of all, the man can tell a story with the best of them. Or, at least, that's what I take from <em>Stardust</em>: A love story in the fantasy realm, done so well it could only have been written by a master of the craft, which is what Neil Gaiman seems to be. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3294209893180208015">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_113564445">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/113564445" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu" class="left imgcol" title="Jason Koivu"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1440701539p2/1742824.jpg" alt="Jason Koivu" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/113564445?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 16, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu" class="user" title="Jason Koivu">Jason Koivu</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/16793.Stardust" title="Paperback 9780061142024" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer113564445">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9497640136672505261"><br />A magically good read! <br /><br /><em>Stardust</em> has been the most fanciful Neil Gaiman book I've read so far. This farcical fantasy might be a tad silly, but he makes it work. I felt drawn to the main characters, repulsed by the villains and enchanted by the story and imagery. It has a bit of an everything-in-the-fantasy-genre-and-the-kitchen-sink feel to it and some might say that many of the elements are not unique. But in my eyes, this is a Gaiman original masterpiece, regardless of what ingredients he used.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/1627194-haley" class="left imgcol" title="Haley"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1224866867p2/1627194.jpg" alt="Haley" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/35835458?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 21, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1627194-haley" class="user" title="Haley">Haley</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/16793.Stardust" title="Paperback 9780061142024" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer35835458">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3633685150331008925">It is my experience that the movie versions of books are usually not as good as the book itself. So after watching the movie, I thought I was in for a real treat.<br />but I was wrong. <br /><br />In Gaiman's defence, this book was written in the style of an old adventure story or Grimm brother's tale- not so much description or character development. But while that sort of writing may work for a short story, It gets old in a full-length book. (though I'm glad it was a book- otherwise we wouldn't have the movie!)</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3633685150331008925">It is my experience that the movie versions of books are usually not as good as the book itself. So after watching the movie, I thought I was in for a real treat.<br />but I was wrong. <br /><br />In Gaiman's defence, this book was written in the style of an old adventure story or Grimm brother's tale- not so much description or character development. But while that sort of writing may work for a short story, It gets old in a full-length book. (though I'm glad it was a book- otherwise we wouldn't have the movie!)<br /><br />Then there's the plot. I like books to be sort of well-thought out, but this one wasn't at all. Tristran and Yvaine are stuck in the clouds- <em> obviously </em> a sky pirate is going to come save them? huh? It would have been better of there had been mention of sky-pirates earlier in the novel, so then it wouldn't seem like Gaiman was having some kind of sporadic writer's block.<br /><br />and there is no confrontation at the end, it's totally anti-climactic. just, "oh, my heart is now Tristrans," and "damn, I guess I can't cut it out of you." -This could actually have been a good ending, maybe if there had been a mentioning of the possibiliy, or even if the witch had caught Yvaine, but was unable to cut her heart out. <br /><br />Also, I was looking forward to reading about the prancing, dancing pirate-captain from the movie, but those few months are condensed into only a few paragraphs. This was an oportunity to have some character development, and to show the romance between Tristran and Yvaine blossoming, because it kind of pops up out of thin air. Yes, we all knew it was going to happen, but that just proves this story is predictable in spite of its fantaclismic twists.<br /><br />All in all, the only reason I finished this book was because I loved the movie.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3633685150331008925">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/5253785-lyn" class="left imgcol" title="Lyn"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1428721461p2/5253785.jpg" alt="Lyn" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/336103486?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 30, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5253785-lyn" class="user" title="Lyn">Lyn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/16793.Stardust" title="Paperback 9780061142024" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer336103486">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4825735990397464032">I have heard Stardust by Neil Gaiman described as a fairy tale told for adults, and I think Gaiman himself said something of the kind. That is as succinct a description as comes close to this very entertaining novel. <br /><br />Actually it is a Faerie tale, since Gaiman depicts a journey into that magical world and the village of Wall, which is a “boundary” between the two worlds. Though the author pays homage to nineteenth century storylines, he eschews the flowery language and opts for more post-modern p</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4825735990397464032">I have heard Stardust by Neil Gaiman described as a fairy tale told for adults, and I think Gaiman himself said something of the kind. That is as succinct a description as comes close to this very entertaining novel. <br /><br />Actually it is a Faerie tale, since Gaiman depicts a journey into that magical world and the village of Wall, which is a “boundary” between the two worlds. Though the author pays homage to nineteenth century storylines, he eschews the flowery language and opts for more post-modern prose to narrate his retrospective, pre-Tolkeinesque fantasy. <br /><br />I can see the comparisons to <a title="The Princess Bride  by William Goldman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21787.The_Princess_Bride_">The Princess Bride</a>, but for reasons that I cannot explain or understand, I frequently found myself thinking of <a title="The Great God Pan by Arthur Machen" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/774846.The_Great_God_Pan">The Great God Pan</a>. <br /><br />All in all, an enjoyable Goodread.<br /><br /><img width="400" height="400" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427763141i/14318749._SY540_.jpg" /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4825735990397464032">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1206867450">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3326817645012683743"><em>"He stared up at the stars: and it seemed to him then that they were dancers, stately and graceful, performing a dance almost infinite in its complexity. He imagined he could see the very faces of the stars; pale, they were, and smiling gently, as if they had spent so much time above the world, watching the scrambling and the joy and the pain of the people below them, that they could not help being amused every time another little human believed itself the center of its world, as each of us does</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3326817645012683743"><em>"He stared up at the stars: and it seemed to him then that they were dancers, stately and graceful, performing a dance almost infinite in its complexity. He imagined he could see the very faces of the stars; pale, they were, and smiling gently, as if they had spent so much time above the world, watching the scrambling and the joy and the pain of the people below them, that they could not help being amused every time another little human believed itself the center of its world, as each of us does."</em><br /><br />When Tristan Thorn makes a rash promise to a beautiful girl he embarks into the world of Faerie and learns that some things (including himself) are not quite what they seem.<br /><br />This is a gorgeously intricate fairy tale for adults. I absolutely love this book, it might just be my favorite Gaiman book and also my favorite fairytale type story. :)</span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1006585133">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10978640764315508824">Wavering between 3 and 4 stars, so I'll settle with 3.5<br /><br />I saw the film years ago before I'd even heard of Neil Gaiman, so I had no idea it was based on a book. The movie is one of my favorites as far as fairy tales go, and after finishing the book, I have to say that it's an excellent modern fairy tale (though very much a mature one, considering it involves sex and violence more so than the fairy tales I grew up with). It's written very much in the vein of Grimm's or Andersen's classic stories, a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10978640764315508824">Wavering between 3 and 4 stars, so I'll settle with 3.5<br /><br />I saw the film years ago before I'd even heard of Neil Gaiman, so I had no idea it was based on a book. The movie is one of my favorites as far as fairy tales go, and after finishing the book, I have to say that it's an excellent modern fairy tale (though very much a mature one, considering it involves sex and violence more so than the fairy tales I grew up with). It's written very much in the vein of Grimm's or Andersen's classic stories, and I love that vibe.<br /><br />Also, have I mentioned how much I love the way Neil reads? I may have to start a collection of his books strictly on audio.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_97549326">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/97549326" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1805180-seak" class="left imgcol" title="seak"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1410456529p2/1805180.jpg" alt="seak" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/97549326?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 07, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1805180-seak" class="user" title="seak">seak</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/222063.Stardust" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780380804559" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=2011" class="actionLinkLite">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer97549326">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9539170636204128244">I've always considered myself a Neil Gaiman fan, but then I realized how can that be? Yes, I watched the movie Stardust and I DID read Good Omens...but wait. I never actually read a book solely by Neil Gaiman. <br /><br />What kind of fan does that make me? A terrible one (if you were wondering about the answer). <br /><br />But now, all that's changed...kinda. I'm still a crappy fan, but a fan nonetheless, one who's actually read a book solely written by the author. This will also not be the last. I loved Stardust.<br /><br />The</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9539170636204128244">I've always considered myself a Neil Gaiman fan, but then I realized how can that be? Yes, I watched the movie Stardust and I DID read Good Omens...but wait. I never actually read a book solely by Neil Gaiman. <br /><br />What kind of fan does that make me? A terrible one (if you were wondering about the answer). <br /><br />But now, all that's changed...kinda. I'm still a crappy fan, but a fan nonetheless, one who's actually read a book solely written by the author. This will also not be the last. I loved Stardust.<br /><br />The best way to describe this book is that it's a modern day fairy tale. It's lyrical, it's magical... whimsical would also work here. And the modern day part is evidenced in that Gaiman doesn't shy away from sex and one hilarious use of profanity. <br /><br />Niel Gaiman is a master.<br /><br /><strong>The Movie</strong><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333793i/693465.jpg" /><br /><br />I can't help but compare the book to the movie. I watched the movie first, so I was constantly comparing throughout, catching the subtle and brilliant uses of foreshadowing. <br /><br />I know plenty of people hated the movie after reading the book, but having been sullied prior to my reading, I thought the movie did a great job capturing the atmosphere and humor of the book. Obviously there are some changes, especially with the ending, but overall the movie stays true to the book.<br /><br />This is a movie I can watch over and over and over again...to my wife's constant chagrin (she's not a big fantasy fan). <br /><br />Why Read Stardust?<br /><br />If you watched the movie and loved it, this will only heighten your enjoyment. It's a quick read and a masterpiece. The movie captures the book impeccably, but it is still well worth your time to read. <br /><br />5 out of 5 Stars </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9539170636204128244">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_210188627">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/210188627" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/520753-kim" class="left imgcol" title="Kim"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1402541317p2/520753.jpg" alt="Kim" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/210188627?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 21, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/520753-kim" class="user" title="Kim">Kim</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/520753-kim?shelf=meh-at-you" class="actionLinkLite">meh-at-you</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/520753-kim?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/520753-kim?shelf=mmxi" class="actionLinkLite">mmxi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer210188627">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10053127831889536989"><br /><em>"There was once a young man who wished to gain his Heart's Desire."</em><br /><br />So it begins. Fine. Yep. These are the stuff fairy tales are made from-blahblahblah. Sure thing. What else you got? <br /><br />I really don’t get the point of this novella. I mean, yes, I see that there once was a man who made a journey to capture the uncapturable (a fallen star) for the woman that he loves. Wait. Does he really love her? Do I really care? I spent half the book thinking his name was Tristan not Trist<strong>r</strong>an, so I guess the answ</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10053127831889536989"><br /><em>"There was once a young man who wished to gain his Heart's Desire."</em><br /><br />So it begins. Fine. Yep. These are the stuff fairy tales are made from-blahblahblah. Sure thing. What else you got? <br /><br />I really don’t get the point of this novella. I mean, yes, I see that there once was a man who made a journey to capture the uncapturable (a fallen star) for the woman that he loves. Wait. Does he really love her? Do I really care? I spent half the book thinking his name was Tristan not Trist<strong>r</strong>an, so I guess the answer is no. Yes, he thinks she’s a hottie. Yes, he stalks her like a bedazzled Margaret Mary Ray rumbling around in Letterman’s bushes. Christ! He sits in trees and watches her undress. What of it? Where is the love? Has he sat down and had coffee with her? Does he know her favorite book? Whether she likes boxers or briefs? Seriously? <br /><br />So, he leaves his boring town of Wall to enter Faerie and find this star who is actually a beautiful young woman.(YAWN) He meets colorful filler characters along the way…yadda yadda yadda. But wait, we have another story line going on about some princely brothers who want to take over their kingdom but have to find a topaz that their father threw out the window, towards that SAME fallen star, before he croaked. And wait, there’s ANOTHER story line where 3 old witch hags also want that fallen star because her heart will given them some much needed youth. SEE HOW THEY INTERCONNECT? <br /><br />Good, because the rest of it is really just a ‘she did this, he did that, they fought, they died, they tricked, he smartens up..’ kind of story. I didn’t really know the characters, I really didn’t care who ended up with who. They all kind of irritated me. The action was pretty dull. What happened to EPIC? Not like ‘dude, that frat party was so epic…’ but like Princess-Bride-Epic or Long-Island-Lolita-Epic… C’mon, Gaiman..bring it on. I know you can do it.. People wouldn’t be so enamored of you if you couldn’t. Right?<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10053127831889536989">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_16288553">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/16288553" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/208149-kevin" class="left imgcol" title="Kevin"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1365703444p2/208149.jpg" alt="Kevin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/16288553?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 05, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/208149-kevin" class="user" title="Kevin">Kevin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/16793.Stardust" title="Paperback 9780061142024" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer16288553">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17581040248729135317">I am becoming something of a Neil Gaiman fan. It started, as much has these days, with my Kindle. I was browsing for some inexpensive books that I could read and stumbled upon Stardust. And just to prove how clueless I can be, I didn't realize this had been made into a movie until after I had finished reading it. I was vaguely aware that the movie had come out but I just never made the connection between the book and movie in my mind (more about my reaction to the movie later.)<br /><br />I enjoyed American</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17581040248729135317">I am becoming something of a Neil Gaiman fan. It started, as much has these days, with my Kindle. I was browsing for some inexpensive books that I could read and stumbled upon Stardust. And just to prove how clueless I can be, I didn't realize this had been made into a movie until after I had finished reading it. I was vaguely aware that the movie had come out but I just never made the connection between the book and movie in my mind (more about my reaction to the movie later.)<br /><br />I enjoyed American Gods but wasn't blown away by it, but I really loved Stardust. While American Gods was long and messy and complex, etc. Stardust was charming, and simple, and nearly perfect. It made me realize why I read stories like this.<br /><br />What is impressive about Stardust is the skill with which Gaiman introduces the characters and settings in order to set up this fairy tale. He has a very light touch that allows him to set up the back story and introduce the reader to this alternate world in a way that piques their curiosity and pulls them in. <br /><br />There are a number of story threads but he weaves them in skillfully so that there is both an action adventure side to it as well as a fairy tale/myth side. That these different dimensions work together and compliment each other says a lot about Gaiman's skills as a writer.<br /><br />And it is also worth noting that he uses an admirable economy of words. The book packs an amazing amount of character development and adventure into less than 300 pages. He has a way of capturing a character's personality with just a short anecdote or description.<br /><br />I really enjoyed the book's tone/voice. It has a sense of humor and is quirky without being campy or slapstick. It is in many ways a beautiful love story, and a deeply romantic one, but there is an ever present sense of tragedy as well. It has a sense of innocence and humility and yet also a sense of deeper knowledge. It captures the excitement and mystery of myths and magical stories and makes you wish you could connect to such a world.<br /><br />Some may think this is just another fairy tale story, but that is easier said than done. It isn't easy to take a well known style, or to use a fancy word: trope, and make it your own; do something both familiar and yet different. Gaiman has pulled this off with style. <br /><br />Stardust was one of those instant favorites. I highly recommend it no matter what your normal reading style or taste. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17581040248729135317">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_327245057">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/327245057" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2112750-farah" class="left imgcol" title="Farah"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1411393917p2/2112750.jpg" alt="Farah" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/327245057?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 02, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2112750-farah" class="user" title="Farah">Farah</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1445892.Stardust_Serbuk_Bintang" title="Paperback 9789792226881" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2112750-farah?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2112750-farah?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2112750-farah?shelf=novel" class="actionLinkLite">novel</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2112750-farah?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer327245057">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6778610088132160162">Dear Neil Gaiman,<br /><s>Anda ganteng.</s><br />Terima kasih sudah menulis kisah luar biasa ini.<br />Dengan jalan cerita yang begitu indah, mendebarkan, cerdas, serta manis jalinannya.<br /><br />Anda benar. Orang dewasa terkadang membutuhkan dongengnya sendiri.<br />Saya, yang saat ini berumur 27 tahun, masih belum sepenuhnya berani mengklaim diri saya sebagai orang dewasa.<br /><br />Ada kalanya saya merasa terperangkap di dalam tubuh berusia 27 tahun, sedangkan jiwa saya masih <em>irresponsible</em> dan <em>childish</em> layaknya anak berusia 14 tahun. <br />Iya, saya</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6778610088132160162">Dear Neil Gaiman,<br /><s>Anda ganteng.</s><br />Terima kasih sudah menulis kisah luar biasa ini.<br />Dengan jalan cerita yang begitu indah, mendebarkan, cerdas, serta manis jalinannya.<br /><br />Anda benar. Orang dewasa terkadang membutuhkan dongengnya sendiri.<br />Saya, yang saat ini berumur 27 tahun, masih belum sepenuhnya berani mengklaim diri saya sebagai orang dewasa.<br /><br />Ada kalanya saya merasa terperangkap di dalam tubuh berusia 27 tahun, sedangkan jiwa saya masih <em>irresponsible</em> dan <em>childish</em> layaknya anak berusia 14 tahun. <br />Iya, saya tidak bisa <em>move on</em>.<br /><br />Tapi rutinitas, <s>permasalahan</s> tantangan hidup, serta keberadaan diri saya di dalam masyarakat telah memaksa saya untuk menumpulkan daya khayal yang dulu pernah saya punya. Pelan-pelan mengikis kebebasan yang dulu pernah ada. Mungkin itu alasannya mengapa akhir-akhir ini membuat review dari buku yang telah saya baca rasanya susah sekali.<br /><br />Satu atau dua tahun lalu, rasanya mudah bagi saya untuk menulis review buku sesuka hati.<br />Saya bisa menginterpretasikan isi buku sesuai yang saya mau. Saya menciptakan percakapan-percakapan imajiner, melanjutkan cerita, menuliskan sesuatu yang tidak untuk dibaca oleh orang lain. <br />Saya pernah menulis hanya untuk diri saya sendiri. Hanya karena saya mau. Dan saya melakukan itu.<br /><br />Kemudian akhir-akhir ini saya juga terbiasa untuk menyusutkan aksara karena keterbatasan karakter yang tersedia di <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.twitter.com/FaraLest">twitter</a>. Percaya atau tidak, saya jadi cenderung menguncupkan ide-ide yang sebenarnya bisa dikembangkan menjadi satu tulisan utuh dan menjejalkan semuanya ke dalam kotak yang hanya bisa menampung 140 karakter tersebut. Kalau itu dirasa kurang, saya bisa sih, memotong-motongnya menjadi beberapa bagian. Tapi tetap saja, setiap bagian itu tidak boleh melebihi 140 karakter. Atau saya harus mengamputasi bagian-bagiannya. Yang mana saja. Supaya tulisan-tulisan mikro itu bisa terpampang di linimasa saya.<br /><br />Mudah sekali ya, menyalahkan dunia orang dewasa?<br />Menyalahkan keterbiasaan, serta mengkambinghitamkan apa yang sudah ada tapi tidak mencari inti dari masalahnya. Lalu bagian mana dari diri saya yang bisa disebut dewasa?<br />Tapi salah seorang sahabat baik saya berkata, ini hanyalah satu fase kehidupan yang perlu saya jalani.<br />Mendengar itu saya tahu, saya tidak bisa tersesat terlalu lama.<br />Saya butuh peta untuk menuntun saya lagi. Kalaupun tidak ada, setidaknya ada remah-remah roti yang sengaja disebarkan untuk menunjukkan jejak melewati arah mana saya bisa lewati.<br /><br />Dear Neil Gaiman. <br />Anda ganteng. Iya, kali ini tidak saya coret kalimat itu.<br />Ada yang pernah bilang, bahwa dalam fiksi, semua harus masuk akal.<br />Cerita yang saya baca malam ini, semuanya masuk akal. Masuk akal di dalam kapasitas cerita fantasi dari dunia lain yang sudah begitu lama saya rindukan untuk saya masuki kembali.<br />Maka buku ini adalah undangan untuk kembali ke dunia itu. Setiap halamannya adalah mural yang merayakan betapa dulu saya pernah memiliki imaji yang besar, tinggi, dari lantai yang saya pijak hingga ke langit-langit yang ternyata tanpa batas.<br /><br />Ini adalah gerbang yang saya masuki, saya beruntung bisa melewatinya sekali lagi.<br />Di dunia ini, ada <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/63661229">Sophie</a>. Yang darinya lah saya berani belajar untuk menuliskan semua kerumitan pola berpikir yang terpengaruh oleh Plato dan Socrates. Karena saya adalah filsuf setengah jadi. <br />Kemudian, saya disambut oleh <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/123324401">si bocah tikus</a>. Senyumnya adalah prasasti yang akan selalu mengingatkan bahwa saya pernah berhasil menulis untuk diri saya sendiri. Melanjutkan cerita yang sudah ada. Bahkan tanpa seijin penulisnya. Bentuk 'kenakalan' saya, daya khayal yang <em>(sebenarnya dari)</em> dulu pernah tidak bisa saya kendalikan. <br />Oh. Muncul juga <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/120418852">pasangan aneh ini.</a> Mereka yang akan selalu mengingatkan saya bahwa apa yang ada di kepala saya pastilah dipengaruhi oleh apa yang saya baca, dan siapa yang menuliskannya.<br />Di ujung perjalanan kilas balik ini, ada <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/120460380">Coraline</a> yang menyambut saya dengan pelukan dan senyum yang menghiasi wajahnya yang selalu penasaran.<br />Ia bertanya, bagaimana perjalanannya.<br />Saya menjawab dengan senyum. Ia tahu, saya merasa hidup lagi.<br /><br />Saya terhempas kembali ke sini. Duduk terdiam sambil memandangi buku di tangan saya ini. <br />Selain memikirkan apa yang harus saya tuliskan disini, puji dan puja apa yang perlu saya sampaikan atas penemuan kembali jati diri ini. Kepada Anda.<br /><br />Saya selalu berpikir tidak mudah untuk menciptakan dunia bagi karakter-karakter yang ingin saya hidupkan. Saya harus membangun sebuah kompleksitas yang terjalin rumit secara ajaib barulah dunia itu bisa juga dimasuki oleh orang yang akan membaca tulisan saya.<br /><br />Percayalah, saat ini pelan-pelan saya sedang menyusun pondasinya. <br />Saya bekerja lagi dari awal diatas puing-puing cerita yang dulu pernah saya hancurkan dengan tangan saya sendiri. Tidak perlu lagi dihitung berapa banyak karakter separuh jadi yang tak sempat lahir. Mereka mati teraborsi.<br /><br />Lihat, saya masih bisa menggunakan pilihan-pilihan kata yang, memang sesuai mau saya, tidak biasa-biasa saja.<br />Oh iya, efek dramatis itu perlu rasanya. Tapi mudah-mudahan kali ini saya tidak lagi terbelit alur cerita sendiri yang rumit bagai benang kusut.<br />Karena ada masanya imajinasi ternyata memerlukan kesederhanaan.<br /><br />Mimpi saya yang dulu saya kira pernah menguap melayang melalui jendela, ternyata hanya terapung-apung di belantara yang terlupa.<br />Saya ingin menjadi sederhana. Tapi juga kompleks.<br />Saya ingin mempertahankan luas inspirasi saya tanpa batas, tapi juga berlaku layaknya orang dewasa.<br />Um, maksudnya gimana ya? Mungkin simpelnya, jangan sampai perilaku kekanakan saya itu terlalu banyak saya tunjukkan di depan khalayak ramai. Kurang lebih seperti itu.<br />Tidak mudah ya?<br />Tidak mengapa. Memang tidak ada yang bilang bahwa menjalani hidup ini akan selalu mudah-mudah saja.<br /><br />Dear Neil Gaiman,<br />Terima kasih telah menarik paksa kesadaran yang dulu pernah terkubur sekian lama.<br />Stardust mengembalikan saya lagi ke dunia. Dunia saya. Dunia yang dulu pernah saya kenal.<br /><br />Salam sayang,<br /><br />Penggemar Anda.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6778610088132160162">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Gx/QjWtvyzBM9m/1rM63cOdxgQ4WeHZahTnUN3Rk0sJ+y+9emb3fysAuG07Sr1HCroZCF1+lMfDvMNGluPEkhw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NzVzkGzNI+/VUyHwBQYM40JB9W0VrrjZvG/HtUPQXvlS4UxDnh83FVmLVUt7Z+pRC7Y2dFxz/3PWZsInj0WovA==')})
  }
